<p>The <b>United States Army</b> (<b>USA</b>) is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Land_warfare" title="Land warfare">land warfare</a> service branch of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">United States Armed Forces</a>. It is one of the seven <a href="/wiki/Uniformed_services_of_the_United_States" title="Uniformed services of the United States">uniformed services of the United States</a>, and is designated as the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_United_States" title="Army of the United States">Army of the United States</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a>, Article 2, Section 2, Clause 1] and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Code" title="United States Code">United States Code</a>, Title 10, Subtitle B, Chapter 301, Section 3001].<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> As the oldest and most senior branch of the U.S. military in order of precedence,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> the modern U.S. Army has its roots in the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Army" title="Continental Army">Continental Army</a>, which was formed (14 June 1775) to fight the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a> (1775–1783)—before the United States of America was established as a country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Army_birth_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Army_birth-11">[11]</a></sup> After the Revolutionary War, the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_the_Confederation" title="Congress of the Confederation">Congress of the Confederation</a> created the United States Army on 3 June 1784 to replace the disbanded Continental Army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Army_LOC_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Army_LOC-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Army_History_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Army_History-13">[13]</a></sup> The United States Army considers itself descended from the Continental Army, and dates its institutional inception from the origin of that armed force in 1775.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Army_birth_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Army_birth-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p><p>As a uniformed <a href="/wiki/Military_service" title="Military service">military service</a>, the U.S. Army is part of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Army" title="United States Department of the Army">Department of the Army</a>, which is one of the three military departments of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">Department of Defense</a>. The U.S. Army is headed by a civilian senior appointed civil servant, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_the_Army" title="United States Secretary of the Army">Secretary of the Army</a> (SECARMY) and by a chief <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_officer" title="Military officer">military officer</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_Staff_of_the_United_States_Army" title="Chief of Staff of the United States Army">Chief of Staff of the Army</a> (CSA) who is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Chiefs_of_Staff" title="Joint Chiefs of Staff">Joint Chiefs of Staff</a>. It is the largest military branch, and in the <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_year#United_States" title="Fiscal year">fiscal year</a> 2017, the projected end strength for the <a href="/wiki/Regular_Army_(United_States)" title="Regular Army (United States)">Regular Army</a> (USA) was 476,000 <a href="/wiki/Soldier" title="Soldier">soldiers</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Army_National_Guard" title="Army National Guard">Army National Guard</a> (ARNG) had 343,000 soldiers and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Reserve" title="United States Army Reserve">United States Army Reserve</a> (USAR) had 199,000 soldiers; the combined-component strength of the U.S. Army was 1,018,000 soldiers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-defense.gov_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-defense.gov-4">[4]</a></sup> As a branch of the armed forces, the mission of the U.S. Army is "to fight and win our Nation's wars, by providing prompt, sustained, land dominance, across the full range of military operations and the spectrum of conflict, in support of combatant commanders".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The branch participates in conflicts worldwide and is the major ground-based offensive and defensive force of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mission">Mission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Mission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The United States Army serves as the land-based branch of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">U.S. Armed Forces</a>. <a class="external text" href="https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/10/3062" rel="nofollow">Section 3062 of Title 10, U.S. Code</a> defines the purpose of the army as:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Preserving the peace and security and providing for the defense of the United States, the Commonwealths and possessions and any areas occupied by the United States</li>
<li>Supporting the national policies</li>
<li>Implementing the national objectives</li>
<li>Overcoming any nations responsible for aggressive acts that imperil the peace and security of the United States</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_Army" title="History of the United States Army">History of the United States Army</a></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-move" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" data-file-height="100" data-file-width="300" height="17" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Split-arrows.svg/50px-Split-arrows.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Split-arrows.svg/75px-Split-arrows.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Split-arrows.svg/100px-Split-arrows.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article or section <b>may need to be cleaned up or summarized</b> because it has been split from/to <i><a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_Army" title="History of the United States Army">History of the United States Army</a></i>.</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bataille_Yorktown.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1373" data-file-width="1909" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Bataille_Yorktown.jpg/220px-Bataille_Yorktown.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Bataille_Yorktown.jpg/330px-Bataille_Yorktown.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Bataille_Yorktown.jpg/440px-Bataille_Yorktown.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bataille_Yorktown.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Storming of Redoubt No. 10 in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Yorktown" title="Siege of Yorktown">Siege of Yorktown</a> during the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a> prompted the British government to begin negotiations, resulting in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">Treaty of Paris</a> and British recognition of the United States of America.</div></div></div>
<p>The Continental Army was created on 14 June 1775 by the <a href="/wiki/Second_Continental_Congress" title="Second Continental Congress">Second Continental Congress</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> as a unified army for the colonies to fight <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a>, with <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a> appointed as its commander.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Army_birth_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-Army_birth-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The army was initially led by men who had served in the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a> or colonial militias and who brought much of British military heritage with them. As the Revolutionary War progressed, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_Modern_France" title="Early Modern France">French</a> aid, resources and military thinking influenced the new army. A number of European soldiers came on their own to help, such as <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Wilhelm_von_Steuben" title="Friedrich Wilhelm von Steuben">Friedrich Wilhelm von Steuben</a>, who taught <a href="/wiki/Prussian_Army" title="Prussian Army">Prussian Army</a> tactics and organizational skills.
</p><p>The army fought numerous pitched battles and in the South in 1780–1781, sometimes used the <a href="/wiki/Fabian_strategy" title="Fabian strategy">Fabian strategy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hit-and-run_tactics" title="Hit-and-run tactics">hit-and-run tactics</a>, hitting where the British were weakest to wear down their forces. Washington led victories against the British at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trenton" title="Battle of Trenton">Trenton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Princeton" title="Battle of Princeton">Princeton</a>, but lost a series of battles in the <a href="/wiki/New_York_and_New_Jersey_campaign" title="New York and New Jersey campaign">New York and New Jersey campaign</a> in 1776 and the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_campaign" title="Philadelphia campaign">Philadelphia campaign</a> in 1777. With a decisive victory at <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Yorktown" title="Siege of Yorktown">Yorktown</a> and the help of the French, the Continental Army prevailed against the British.
</p><p>After the war, the Continental Army was quickly given land certificates and disbanded in a reflection of the <a href="/wiki/Republicanism_in_the_United_States" title="Republicanism in the United States">republican</a> distrust of standing armies. State militias became the new nation's sole ground army, with the exception of <a href="/wiki/First_American_Regiment" title="First American Regiment">a regiment</a> to guard the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territory" title="Northwest Territory">Western Frontier</a> and one battery of artillery guarding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Point" title="West Point">West Point</a>'s arsenal. However, because of continuing conflict with <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native Americans</a>, it was soon realized that it was necessary to field a trained standing army. The <a href="/wiki/Regular_Army_(United_States)" title="Regular Army (United States)">Regular Army</a> was at first very small and after General <a href="/wiki/St._Clair%27s_Defeat" title="St. Clair's Defeat">St. Clair's defeat</a> at the Battle of the Wabash, the Regular Army was reorganized as the <a href="/wiki/Legion_of_the_United_States" title="Legion of the United States">Legion of the United States</a>, which was established in 1791 and renamed the United States Army in 1796.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_wars_on_the_Frontier">Early wars on the Frontier</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Early wars on the Frontier">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Army_on_the_Frontier" title="Army on the Frontier">Army on the Frontier</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_New_Orleans.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2579" data-file-width="3488" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Battle_of_New_Orleans.jpg/220px-Battle_of_New_Orleans.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Battle_of_New_Orleans.jpg/330px-Battle_of_New_Orleans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Battle_of_New_Orleans.jpg/440px-Battle_of_New_Orleans.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_New_Orleans.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>General <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Jackson" title="Andrew Jackson">Andrew Jackson</a> stands on the parapet of his makeshift defenses as his troops repulse attacking <a href="/wiki/93rd_(Sutherland_Highlanders)_Regiment_of_Foot" title="93rd (Sutherland Highlanders) Regiment of Foot">Highlanders</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_New_Orleans" title="Battle of New Orleans">defense of New Orleans</a>, the final major and most one-sided battle of the War of 1812</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>, the second and last war between the United States and Great Britain, had mixed results.  The U.S. Army did not conquer Canada but it did destroy Native American resistance to expansion in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Northwest" title="Old Northwest">Old Northwest</a> and it validated its independence by stopping two major British invasions in 1814 and 1815. After <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lake_Erie" title="Battle of Lake Erie">taking control of Lake Erie</a> in 1813, the U.S. Army seized parts of western Upper Canada, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_York" title="Battle of York">burned York</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Thames" title="Battle of the Thames">defeated Tecumseh</a>, which caused his <a href="/wiki/Western_Confederacy" title="Western Confederacy">Western Confederacy</a> to collapse. Following U.S. victories in the Canadian province of Upper Canada, British troops who had dubbed the U.S. Army "Regulars, by God!", were able to capture and <a href="/wiki/Burning_of_Washington" title="Burning of Washington">burn Washington</a>, which was defended by militia, in 1814. The regular army, however proved they were professional and capable of defeating the British army during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Plattsburgh" title="Battle of Plattsburgh">invasions of Plattsburgh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Baltimore" title="Battle of Baltimore">Baltimore</a>, prompting British agreement on the previously rejected terms of a <a href="/wiki/Status_quo" title="Status quo">status quo</a> ante bellum. Two weeks after a treaty was signed (but not ratified), <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Jackson" title="Andrew Jackson">Andrew Jackson</a> defeated the British in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_New_Orleans" title="Battle of New Orleans">Battle of New Orleans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Fort_St._Philip_(1815)" title="Siege of Fort St. Philip (1815)">Siege of Fort St. Philip</a>, and became a national hero. U.S. troops and sailors <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_HMS_Cyane_and_HMS_Levant" title="Capture of HMS Cyane and HMS Levant">captured HMS Cyane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_HMS_Cyane_and_HMS_Levant" title="Capture of HMS Cyane and HMS Levant">Levant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_HMS_Cyane_and_HMS_Levant" title="Capture of HMS Cyane and HMS Levant">Penguin</a> in the final engagements of the war. Per the treaty, both sides (the United States and Great Britain) returned to the geographical status quo. Both navies kept the warships they had seized during the conflict.
</p><p>The army's major campaign against the Indians was fought in <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> against <a href="/wiki/Seminole" title="Seminole">Seminoles</a>. It took long wars (1818–1858) to finally defeat the Seminoles and move them to Oklahoma. The usual strategy in Indian wars was to seize control of the Indians' winter food supply, but that was no use in Florida where there was no winter. The second strategy was to form alliances with other Indian tribes, but that too was useless because the Seminoles had destroyed all the other Indians when they entered Florida in the late eighteenth century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p><p>The U.S. Army fought and won the <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">Mexican–American War</a> (1846–1848), which was a defining event for both countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The U.S. victory resulted in acquisition of territory that eventually became all or parts of the states of <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Civil_War">American Civil War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: American Civil War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Union_Army" title="Union Army">Union Army</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thure_de_Thulstrup_-_L._Prang_and_Co._-_Battle_of_Gettysburg_-_Restoration_by_Adam_Cuerden.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="7000" data-file-width="9656" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Thure_de_Thulstrup_-_L._Prang_and_Co._-_Battle_of_Gettysburg_-_Restoration_by_Adam_Cuerden.jpg/220px-Thure_de_Thulstrup_-_L._Prang_and_Co._-_Battle_of_Gettysburg_-_Restoration_by_Adam_Cuerden.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Thure_de_Thulstrup_-_L._Prang_and_Co._-_Battle_of_Gettysburg_-_Restoration_by_Adam_Cuerden.jpg/330px-Thure_de_Thulstrup_-_L._Prang_and_Co._-_Battle_of_Gettysburg_-_Restoration_by_Adam_Cuerden.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Thure_de_Thulstrup_-_L._Prang_and_Co._-_Battle_of_Gettysburg_-_Restoration_by_Adam_Cuerden.jpg/440px-Thure_de_Thulstrup_-_L._Prang_and_Co._-_Battle_of_Gettysburg_-_Restoration_by_Adam_Cuerden.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thure_de_Thulstrup_-_L._Prang_and_Co._-_Battle_of_Gettysburg_-_Restoration_by_Adam_Cuerden.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gettysburg" title="Battle of Gettysburg">Battle of Gettysburg</a>, the turning point of the American Civil War</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> was the costliest war for the U.S. in terms of casualties. After most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_state" title="Slave state">slave states</a>, located in the southern U.S., formed the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederate States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_Army" title="Confederate States Army">Confederate States Army</a>, led by former U.S. Army officers, mobilized a large fraction of Southern white manpower. Forces of the United States (the "Union" or "the North") formed the <a href="/wiki/Union_Army" title="Union Army">Union Army</a>, consisting of a small body of regular army units and a large body of volunteer units raised from every state, north and south, except <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>For the first two years Confederate forces did well in set battles but lost control of the border states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The Confederates had the advantage of defending a large territory in an area where disease caused twice as many deaths as combat. The Union pursued a strategy of seizing the coastline, blockading the ports, and taking control of the river systems. By 1863, the Confederacy was being strangled. Its eastern armies fought well, but the western armies were defeated one after another until the Union forces captured New Orleans in 1862 along with the Tennessee River.  In the <a href="/wiki/Vicksburg_Campaign" title="Vicksburg Campaign">Vicksburg Campaign</a> of 1862–1863, General <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ulysses_Grant" title="Ulysses Grant">Ulysses Grant</a> seized the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a> and cut off the Southwest.  Grant took command of Union forces in 1864 and after a series of battles with very heavy casualties, he had General <a href="/wiki/Robert_E._Lee" title="Robert E. Lee">Robert E. Lee</a> under siege in Richmond as General <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_T._Sherman" title="William T. Sherman">William T. Sherman</a> captured Atlanta and marched through Georgia and <a href="/wiki/The_Carolinas" title="The Carolinas">the Carolinas</a>.  The Confederate capital was abandoned in April 1865 and Lee subsequently surrendered his army at Appomattox Court House. All other Confederate armies surrendered within a few months.
</p><p>The war remains the deadliest conflict in U.S. history, resulting in the deaths of 620,000 men on both sides. Based on 1860 census figures, 8% of all white males aged 13 to 43 died in the war, including 6.4% in <a href="/wiki/Northern_United_States" title="Northern United States">the North</a> and 18% in <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">the South</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_19th_century">Later 19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Later 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Soldiers_of_1890.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="299" data-file-width="413" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Soldiers_of_1890.jpg/220px-Soldiers_of_1890.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Soldiers_of_1890.jpg/330px-Soldiers_of_1890.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e3/Soldiers_of_1890.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Soldiers_of_1890.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Army soldiers in 1890</div></div></div>
<p>Following the Civil War, the U.S. Army had the mission of containing western tribes of Native Americans on the <a href="/wiki/Indian_reservation" title="Indian reservation">Indian reservations</a>. They set up many forts, and engaged in the last of the <a href="/wiki/American_Indian_Wars" title="American Indian Wars">American Indian Wars</a>. U.S. Army troops also occupied several Southern states during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reconstruction_Era" title="Reconstruction Era">Reconstruction Era</a> to protect <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedmen" title="Freedmen">freedmen</a>.
</p><p>The key battles of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a> of 1898 were fought by the Navy. Using mostly new volunteers, the U.S. Army defeated <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> in land campaigns in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and played the central role in the <a href="/wiki/Philippine%E2%80%93American_War" title="Philippine–American War">Philippine–American War</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:At_close_grips2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1781" data-file-width="1834" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/At_close_grips2.jpg/220px-At_close_grips2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/At_close_grips2.jpg/330px-At_close_grips2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/At_close_grips2.jpg/440px-At_close_grips2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:At_close_grips2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. Army troops assault a German bunker, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, c. 1918</div></div></div>
<p>Starting in 1910, the army began acquiring <a href="/wiki/Fixed-wing_aircraft" title="Fixed-wing aircraft">fixed-wing aircraft</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> In 1910, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> was having a civil war, peasant rebels fighting government soldiers. The army was deployed to U.S. towns near the border to ensure safety to lives and property. In 1916, <a href="/wiki/Pancho_Villa" title="Pancho Villa">Pancho Villa</a>, a major rebel leader, attacked <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_New_Mexico" title="Columbus, New Mexico">Columbus, New Mexico</a>, prompting a <a href="/wiki/Pancho_Villa_Expedition" title="Pancho Villa Expedition">U.S. intervention in Mexico</a> until 7 February 1917. They fought the rebels and the Mexican federal troops until 1918.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_wars">World wars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: World wars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For a list of campaigns see <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Army_campaigns_during_World_War_II" title="List of United States Army campaigns during World War II">List of United States Army campaigns during World War II</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/American_entry_into_World_War_I" title="American entry into World War I">United States joined World War I</a> as an "Associated Power" in 1917 on the side of <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britain</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Italy</a> and the other <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allies</a>. U.S. troops were sent to the <a href="/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_I)" title="Western Front (World War I)">Western Front</a> and were involved in the last offensives that ended the war. With the armistice in November 1918, the army once again decreased its forces.
</p><p>In 1939, estimates of the Army's strength range between 174,000 and 200,000 soldiers, smaller than that of <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>'s, which ranked it 17th or 19th in the world in size. General <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_C._Marshall" title="George C. Marshall">George C. Marshall</a> became Army Chief of Staff in September 1939 and set about expanding and modernizing the Army in preparation for war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:U.S._Soldiers_at_Bougainville_(Solomon_Islands)_March_1944.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2325" data-file-width="3000" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/U.S._Soldiers_at_Bougainville_%28Solomon_Islands%29_March_1944.jpg/220px-U.S._Soldiers_at_Bougainville_%28Solomon_Islands%29_March_1944.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/U.S._Soldiers_at_Bougainville_%28Solomon_Islands%29_March_1944.jpg/330px-U.S._Soldiers_at_Bougainville_%28Solomon_Islands%29_March_1944.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/U.S._Soldiers_at_Bougainville_%28Solomon_Islands%29_March_1944.jpg/440px-U.S._Soldiers_at_Bougainville_%28Solomon_Islands%29_March_1944.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:U.S._Soldiers_at_Bougainville_(Solomon_Islands)_March_1944.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. soldiers hunt Japanese infiltrators during the <a href="/wiki/Bougainville_Campaign" title="Bougainville Campaign">Bougainville Campaign</a></div></div></div>
<p>The United States joined <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> in December 1941 after the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japanese</a> <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attack on Pearl Harbor</a>. On the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Theatre_of_World_War_II" title="European Theatre of World War II">European front</a>, U.S. Army troops formed a significant portion of the forces that captured <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tunisia_Campaign" title="Tunisia Campaign">North Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Allied_invasion_of_Sicily" title="Allied invasion of Sicily">Sicily</a> and later fought in <a href="/wiki/Italian_Campaign_(World_War_II)" title="Italian Campaign (World War II)">Italy</a>. On <a href="/wiki/Normandy_landings" title="Normandy landings">D-Day</a> 6 June 1944 and in the subsequent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_Front" title="Second Front">liberation of Europe</a> and defeat of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>, millions of U.S. Army troops played a central role. In the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_War" title="Pacific War">Pacific War</a>, U.S. Army soldiers participated alongside the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">United States Marine Corps</a> in capturing the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands" title="Pacific Islands">Pacific Islands</a> from Japanese control. Following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" title="Axis Powers">Axis</a> surrenders in May (Germany) and August (Japan) of 1945, army troops were deployed to Japan and Germany to occupy the two defeated nations. Two years after World War II, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Army_Air_Forces" title="Army Air Forces">Army Air Forces</a> separated from the army to become the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">United States Air Force</a> in September 1947. In 1948, the army was <a href="/wiki/Desegregation" title="Desegregation">desegregated</a> by <a href="/wiki/Executive_Order_9981" title="Executive Order 9981">order</a> of President <a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman" title="Harry S. Truman">Harry S. Truman</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cold_War">Cold War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Cold War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<h5><span id="1945.E2.80.931960"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1945–1960">1945–1960</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 1945–1960">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Exercise_Desert_Rock_I_(Buster-Jangle_Dog)_003.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="332" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Exercise_Desert_Rock_I_%28Buster-Jangle_Dog%29_003.jpg/170px-Exercise_Desert_Rock_I_%28Buster-Jangle_Dog%29_003.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Exercise_Desert_Rock_I_%28Buster-Jangle_Dog%29_003.jpg/255px-Exercise_Desert_Rock_I_%28Buster-Jangle_Dog%29_003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/41/Exercise_Desert_Rock_I_%28Buster-Jangle_Dog%29_003.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Exercise_Desert_Rock_I_(Buster-Jangle_Dog)_003.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. Army soldiers look on an atomic bomb test of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Buster-Jangle" title="Operation Buster-Jangle">Operation Buster-Jangle</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Nevada_Test_Site" title="Nevada Test Site">Nevada Test Site</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The end of World War II set the stage for the East–West confrontation known as the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. With the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>, concerns over the defense of Western Europe rose. Two corps, <a href="/wiki/V_Corps_(United_States)" title="V Corps (United States)">V</a> and <a href="/wiki/VII_Corps_(United_States)" title="VII Corps (United States)">VII</a>, were reactivated under <a href="/wiki/Seventh_United_States_Army" title="Seventh United States Army">Seventh United States Army</a> in 1950 and U.S. strength in Europe rose from one division to four. Hundreds of thousands of U.S. troops remained stationed in West Germany, with others in <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, until the 1990s in anticipation of a possible <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> attack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PerkinsAOC_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-PerkinsAOC-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>minute 9:00-10:00</span></sup>
</p><p>During the Cold War, U.S. troops and their allies fought <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">communist</a> forces in Korea and <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>. The Korean War began in 1950, when the Soviets walked out of a U.N. Security Council meeting, removing their possible veto. Under a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> umbrella, hundreds of thousands of U.S. troops fought to prevent the takeover of <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> by <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> and later to invade the northern nation. After repeated advances and retreats by both sides and the Chinese <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Volunteer_Army" title="People's Volunteer Army">People's Volunteer Army</a>'s entry into the war, the <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Korean_Armistice_Agreement" title="s:Korean Armistice Agreement">Korean Armistice Agreement</a> returned the peninsula to the status quo in 1953.
</p>
<h5><span id="1960.E2.80.931970"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1960–1970">1960–1970</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 1960–1970">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> is often regarded as a low point for the U.S. Army due to the use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Draft" title="The Draft">drafted personnel</a>, the unpopularity of the war with the U.S. public and frustrating restrictions placed on the military by U.S. political leaders. While U.S. forces had been stationed in <a href="/wiki/South_Vietnam" title="South Vietnam">South Vietnam</a> since 1959, in intelligence and advising/training roles, they were not deployed in large numbers until 1965, after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Tonkin_Incident" title="Gulf of Tonkin Incident">Gulf of Tonkin Incident</a>. U.S. forces effectively established and maintained control of the "traditional" battlefield, but they struggled to counter the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guerrilla_war" title="Guerrilla war">guerrilla</a> hit and run tactics of the communist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Front_for_the_Liberation_of_South_Vietnam" title="National Front for the Liberation of South Vietnam">Viet Cong</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vietnam_People%27s_Army" title="Vietnam People's Army">North Vietnamese Army</a>. On a tactical level, U.S. soldiers (and the U.S. military as a whole) did not lose a sizable battle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DakToVietnam1966.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1718" data-file-width="2578" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/DakToVietnam1966.jpg/220px-DakToVietnam1966.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/DakToVietnam1966.jpg/330px-DakToVietnam1966.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/DakToVietnam1966.jpg/440px-DakToVietnam1966.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DakToVietnam1966.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A U.S. Army infantry patrol moves up to assault the last <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Vietnamese_Army" title="North Vietnamese Army">North Vietnamese Army</a> position at Dak To, South Vietnam during Operation Hawthorne</div></div></div>
<p>During the 1960s, the Department of Defense continued to scrutinize the reserve forces and to question the number of divisions and brigades as well as the redundancy of maintaining two reserve components, the <a href="/wiki/Army_National_Guard" title="Army National Guard">Army National Guard</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Reserve" title="United States Army Reserve">Army Reserve</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> In 1967, Secretary of Defense <a href="/wiki/Robert_McNamara" title="Robert McNamara">Robert McNamara</a> decided that 15 combat divisions in the Army National Guard were unnecessary and cut the number to eight divisions (one mechanized infantry, two armored, and five infantry), but increased the number of brigades from seven to 18 (one airborne, one armored, two mechanized infantry and 14 infantry). The loss of the divisions did not sit well with the states. Their objections included the inadequate maneuver element mix for those that remained and the end to the practice of rotating divisional commands among the states that supported them. Under the proposal, the remaining division commanders were to reside in the state of the division base. However, no reduction in total Army National Guard strength was to take place, which convinced the governors to accept the plan. The states reorganized their forces accordingly between 1 December 1967 and 1 May 1968.
</p>
<h5><span id="1970.E2.80.931990"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1970–1990">1970–1990</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 1970–1990">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Operation_Just_Cause_Rangers_3rd_sqd_la_comadancia_small.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="198" data-file-width="288" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Operation_Just_Cause_Rangers_3rd_sqd_la_comadancia_small.jpg/220px-Operation_Just_Cause_Rangers_3rd_sqd_la_comadancia_small.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c0/Operation_Just_Cause_Rangers_3rd_sqd_la_comadancia_small.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Operation_Just_Cause_Rangers_3rd_sqd_la_comadancia_small.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. Army soldiers prepare to take <i>La Comandancia</i> in the <i>El Chorrillo neighborhood</i> of <a href="/wiki/Panama_City" title="Panama City">Panama City</a> during the <a href="/wiki/United_States_invasion_of_Panama" title="United States invasion of Panama">United States invasion of Panama</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Total Force Policy was adopted by Chief of Staff of the Army General <a href="/wiki/Creighton_Abrams" title="Creighton Abrams">Creighton Abrams</a> in the aftermath of the Vietnam War and involves treating the three components of the army – the <a href="/wiki/Regular_Army_(United_States)" title="Regular Army (United States)">Regular Army</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Army_National_Guard" title="Army National Guard">Army National Guard</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Reserve" title="United States Army Reserve">Army Reserve</a> as a single force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Army_National_Guard_Constitution_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Army_National_Guard_Constitution-32">[32]</a></sup> Believing that no U.S. President should be able to take the United States (and more specifically the U.S. Army) to war without the support of the U.S. people, General Abrams intertwined the structure of the three components of the army in such a way as to make extended operations impossible, without the involvement of both the Army National Guard and the Army Reserve.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup>
</p><p>The 1980s was mostly a decade of reorganization. The army converted to an all-volunteer force with greater emphasis on training and technology. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Goldwater-Nichols_Act" title="Goldwater-Nichols Act">Goldwater-Nichols Act</a> of 1986 created <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unified_Combatant_Command" title="Unified Combatant Command">unified combatant commands</a> bringing the army together with the other four <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Military" title="United States Military">military services</a> under unified, geographically organized command structures. The army also played a role in the invasions of <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a> in 1983 (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Grenada" title="Invasion of Grenada">Operation Urgent Fury</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a> in 1989 (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Just_Cause" title="Operation Just Cause">Operation Just Cause</a>).
</p><p>By 1989 <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">Germany was nearing reunification</a> and the Cold War was coming to a close. Army leadership reacted by starting to plan for a reduction in strength. By November 1989 Pentagon briefers were laying out plans to reduce army end strength by 23%, from 750,000 to 580,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> A number of incentives such as early retirement were used.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s">1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Abrams_in_formation.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1860" data-file-width="2790" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Abrams_in_formation.jpg/220px-Abrams_in_formation.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Abrams_in_formation.jpg/330px-Abrams_in_formation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Abrams_in_formation.jpg/440px-Abrams_in_formation.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Abrams_in_formation.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/M1_Abrams" title="M1 Abrams">M1 Abrams</a> move out before the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Al_Busayyah" title="Battle of Al Busayyah">Battle of Al Busayyah</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 1990, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Kuwait" title="Invasion of Kuwait">invaded</a> its smaller neighbor, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, and U.S. land forces quickly deployed to assure the protection of <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>. In January 1991 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Desert_Storm" title="Operation Desert Storm">Operation Desert Storm</a> commenced, a U.S.-led coalition which deployed over 500,000 troops, the bulk of them from U.S. Army formations, to <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">drive out Iraqi forces</a>. The campaign ended in total victory, as Western coalition forces routed the <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Army" title="Iraqi Army">Iraqi Army</a>. Some of the largest tank battles in history were fought during the Gulf war. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Medina_Ridge" title="Battle of Medina Ridge">Battle of Medina Ridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Norfolk" title="Battle of Norfolk">Battle of Norfolk</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_73_Easting" title="Battle of 73 Easting">Battle of 73 Easting</a> were tank battles of historical significance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Destroyed_Iraqi_tank_TF-41.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="736" data-file-width="916" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Destroyed_Iraqi_tank_TF-41.jpg/220px-Destroyed_Iraqi_tank_TF-41.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Destroyed_Iraqi_tank_TF-41.jpg/330px-Destroyed_Iraqi_tank_TF-41.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Destroyed_Iraqi_tank_TF-41.jpg/440px-Destroyed_Iraqi_tank_TF-41.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Destroyed_Iraqi_tank_TF-41.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Iraqi tanks destroyed by <a href="/wiki/Task_Force_1-41_Infantry" title="Task Force 1-41 Infantry">Task Force 1-41 Infantry</a> during the 1st Gulf War, February 1991.</div></div></div>
<p>After Operation Desert Storm, the army did not see major combat operations for the remainder of the 1990s but did participate in a number of peacekeeping activities. In 1990 the Department of Defense issued guidance for "rebalancing" after a review of the Total Force Policy,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> but in 2004, <a href="/wiki/Air_War_College" title="Air War College">Air War College</a> scholars concluded the guidance would reverse the Total Force Policy which is an "essential ingredient to the successful application of military force."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_DVIDSHUB_-_Operation_in_Nahr-e_Saraj_(Image_5_of_7).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2392" data-file-width="4914" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Flickr_-_DVIDSHUB_-_Operation_in_Nahr-e_Saraj_%28Image_5_of_7%29.jpg/220px-Flickr_-_DVIDSHUB_-_Operation_in_Nahr-e_Saraj_%28Image_5_of_7%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Flickr_-_DVIDSHUB_-_Operation_in_Nahr-e_Saraj_%28Image_5_of_7%29.jpg/330px-Flickr_-_DVIDSHUB_-_Operation_in_Nahr-e_Saraj_%28Image_5_of_7%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Flickr_-_DVIDSHUB_-_Operation_in_Nahr-e_Saraj_%28Image_5_of_7%29.jpg/440px-Flickr_-_DVIDSHUB_-_Operation_in_Nahr-e_Saraj_%28Image_5_of_7%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_DVIDSHUB_-_Operation_in_Nahr-e_Saraj_(Image_5_of_7).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Army Rangers take part in a raid during operation in Nahr-e Saraj, Afghanistan</div></div></div>
<p>On 11 September 2001, 53 Army civilians (47 employees and six contractors) and 22 soldiers were among the 125 victims killed in <a href="/wiki/The_Pentagon" title="The Pentagon">the Pentagon</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">terrorist attack</a> when <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines_Flight_77" title="American Airlines Flight 77">American Airlines Flight 77</a> commandeered by five <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">Al-Qaeda</a> <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_hijacking" title="Aircraft hijacking">hijackers</a> slammed into the western side of the building, as part of the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_general_(United_States)" title="Lieutenant general (United States)">Lieutenant General</a> <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Maude" title="Timothy Maude">Timothy Maude</a> was the highest-ranking military official killed at the Pentagon and the most senior U.S. Army officer killed by foreign action since the death of Lieutenant General <a href="/wiki/Simon_Bolivar_Buckner_Jr." title="Simon Bolivar Buckner Jr.">Simon B. Buckner Jr.</a> on 18 June 1945 in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Okinawa" title="Battle of Okinawa">Battle of Okinawa</a> during World War II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BarawalaKalay.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="418" data-file-width="626" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/BarawalaKalay.jpg/220px-BarawalaKalay.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/BarawalaKalay.jpg/330px-BarawalaKalay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/BarawalaKalay.jpg/440px-BarawalaKalay.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BarawalaKalay.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. Army soldiers with 2nd Battalion, 327th Infantry Regiment, <a href="/wiki/101st_Airborne_Division" title="101st Airborne Division">101st Airborne Division</a> return fire during a firefight with Taliban forces in Barawala Kalay Valley in Kunar province, Afghanistan, March 2011</div></div></div>
<p>In response to the 11 September attacks and as part of the <a href="/wiki/War_on_Terror" title="War on Terror">Global War on Terror</a>, U.S. and <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> forces <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%9314)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–14)">invaded Afghanistan</a> in October 2001, displacing the <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a> government. The U.S. Army also led the combined U.S. and allied <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">invasion of Iraq</a> in 2003. It served as the primary source for ground forces with its ability to sustain short and long-term deployment operations. In the following years, the mission changed from conflict between regular militaries to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Counterinsurgency" title="Counterinsurgency">counterinsurgency</a>, resulting in the deaths of more than 4,000 U.S. service members (as of March 2008) and injuries to thousands more.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet_supplement_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet_supplement-43">[43]</a></sup> 23,813 insurgents were killed in Iraq between 2003–2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>
</p><p>Until 2009, the army's chief modernization plan, its most ambitious since World War II,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> was the <a href="/wiki/Future_Combat_Systems" title="Future Combat Systems">FCS program</a>. In 2009, many systems were canceled and the remaining were swept into the <a href="/wiki/BCT_Modernization" title="BCT Modernization">BCT modernization program</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> In response to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Budget_sequestration_in_2013" title="Budget sequestration in 2013">Budget sequestration in 2013</a>, the army is planned to shrink to a size not seen since the World War II buildup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> From 2016 to 2017, the army retired hundreds of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OH-58_Kiowa_Warrior" title="OH-58 Kiowa Warrior">OH-58 Kiowa Warrior</a> observation helicopters without an adequate successor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-retired_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-retired-48">[48]</a></sup> The 2015 expenditure for Army research, development and acquisition changed from $32 billion projected in 2012 for FY15 to $21 billion for FY15 expected in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Drw_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Drw-49">[49]</a></sup> By 2017, the Brigade Modernization project was completed and its headquarters, the Brigade Modernization Command, was renamed the Joint Modernization Command, or JMC, to reflect its evolving mission at TRADOC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> (TRADOC is the Army Command whose mission is to define the architecture and organization of the Army, to train and supply soldiers to FORSCOM and to design hardware, as well as to define materiel for AMC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>minutes 2:30-15:00</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PerkinsAOC_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-PerkinsAOC-29">[29]</a></sup>
In 2018 <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Futures_Command" title="United States Army Futures Command">Army Futures Command</a> (AFC) was established as a peer of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FORSCOM" title="FORSCOM">FORSCOM</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TRADOC" title="TRADOC">TRADOC</a>, and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Materiel_Command" title="United States Army Materiel Command">Army Materiel Command</a> (AMC), the other Army commands (ACOMs).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AR10-87_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-AR10-87-52">[52]</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Futures_Command#Cross-functional_teams_(CFTs)" title="United States Army Futures Command">AFC's cross-functional teams (CFTs)</a> are Futures Command's vehicle for sustainable  <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Futures_Command#Need_for_modernization_reform" title="United States Army Futures Command">reform of the acquisition process</a> for the future.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">Organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Structure_of_the_United_States_Army" title="Structure of the United States Army">Structure of the United States Army</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DA_Pam_10-1_Figure_1-1.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="397" data-file-width="649" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/DA_Pam_10-1_Figure_1-1.png/310px-DA_Pam_10-1_Figure_1-1.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/DA_Pam_10-1_Figure_1-1.png/465px-DA_Pam_10-1_Figure_1-1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/DA_Pam_10-1_Figure_1-1.png/620px-DA_Pam_10-1_Figure_1-1.png 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DA_Pam_10-1_Figure_1-1.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. Army organization chart<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Army_components">Army components</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Army components">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The task of organizing the U.S. Army commenced in 1775.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> In the first one hundred years of its existence, the United States Army was maintained as a small peacetime force to man permanent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forts" title="Forts">forts</a> and perform other non-wartime duties such as <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Corps_of_Engineers" title="United States Army Corps of Engineers">engineering</a> and construction works. During times of war, the U.S. Army was augmented by the much larger <a href="/wiki/United_States_Volunteers" title="United States Volunteers">United States Volunteers</a> which were raised independently by various state governments. States also maintained full-time <a href="/wiki/Militia" title="Militia">militias</a> which could also be called into the service of the army.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:American_World_War_II_senior_military_officials,_1945.JPEG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2264" data-file-width="2837" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/American_World_War_II_senior_military_officials%2C_1945.JPEG/220px-American_World_War_II_senior_military_officials%2C_1945.JPEG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/American_World_War_II_senior_military_officials%2C_1945.JPEG/330px-American_World_War_II_senior_military_officials%2C_1945.JPEG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/American_World_War_II_senior_military_officials%2C_1945.JPEG/440px-American_World_War_II_senior_military_officials%2C_1945.JPEG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:American_World_War_II_senior_military_officials,_1945.JPEG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. general officers, World War II, Europe</div></div></div>
<p>By the twentieth century, the U.S. Army had mobilized the U.S. Volunteers on four separate occasions during each of the major wars of the nineteenth century. During World War I, the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Army_(USA)" title="National Army (USA)">National Army</a>" was organized to fight the conflict, replacing the concept of U.S. Volunteers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-55">[55]</a></sup> It was demobilized at the end of World War I, and was replaced by the Regular Army, the Organized Reserve Corps and the State Militias. In the 1920s and 1930s, the "career" soldiers were known as the "<a href="/wiki/Regular_Army_(United_States)" title="Regular Army (United States)">Regular Army</a>" with the "Enlisted Reserve Corps" and "Officer Reserve Corps" augmented to fill vacancies when needed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1941, the "<a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_United_States" title="Army of the United States">Army of the United States</a>" was founded to fight World War II. The Regular Army, Army of the United States, the National Guard and Officer/Enlisted Reserve Corps (ORC and ERC) existed simultaneously. After World War II, the ORC and ERC were combined into the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Reserve" title="United States Army Reserve">United States Army Reserve</a>. The Army of the United States was re-established for the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> and was demobilized upon the suspension of the <a href="/wiki/Conscription_in_the_United_States" title="Conscription in the United States">draft</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>Currently, the Army is divided into the <a href="/wiki/Regular_Army_(United_States)" title="Regular Army (United States)">Regular Army</a>, the Army Reserve and the <a href="/wiki/Army_National_Guard" title="Army National Guard">Army National Guard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-55">[55]</a></sup>  Some states further maintain <a href="/wiki/State_defense_force" title="State defense force">state defense forces</a>, as a type of reserve to the National Guard, while all states maintain regulations for <a href="/wiki/Militia_(United_States)" title="Militia (United States)">state militias</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> State militias are both "organized", meaning that they are armed forces usually part of the state defense forces, or "unorganized" simply meaning that all able bodied males may be eligible to be called into military service.
</p><p>The U.S. Army is also divided into <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Army_careers" title="List of United States Army careers">several branches and functional areas</a>.  Branches include officers, warrant officers, and enlisted Soldiers while functional areas consist of officers who are reclassified from their former branch into a functional area. However, officers continue to wear the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_branch_insignia" title="United States Army branch insignia">branch insignia</a> of their former branch in most cases, as functional areas do not generally have discrete insignia. Some branches, such as Special Forces, operate similarly to functional areas in that individuals may not join their ranks until having served in another Army branch. Careers in the Army can extend into cross-functional areas for officer,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AACSL_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-AACSL-58">[58]</a></sup> warrant officer, enlisted, and civilian personnel.
</p>

<td>Behavioral Sciences (FA 73)
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<p>Before 1933, members of the Army National Guard were considered state militia until they were mobilized into U.S. Army, typically on the onset of war. Since the 1933 amendment to the <a href="/wiki/National_Defense_Act_of_1916" title="National Defense Act of 1916">National Defense Act of 1916</a>, all Army National Guard soldiers have held dual status. They serve as National Guardsmen under the authority of the governor of their state or territory and as a reserve members of the U.S. Army under the authority of the President, in the Army National Guard of the United States.
</p><p>Since the adoption of the total force policy, in the aftermath of the Vietnam War, reserve component soldiers have taken a more active role in U.S. military operations. For example, Reserve and Guard units took part in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a>, peacekeeping in <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, Afghanistan and the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a>.
</p>
